I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
MemoryEventStore: panic "no progress during purge" when first chunk per stream is empty (SSE priming Append(nil))
**Describe the bug**

`MemoryEventStore.purge()` can panic with `panic: no progress during purge` when the store is over `MaxBytes` and a purge pass only removes **leading empty** chunks (`[]byte` / `nil` with length 0). Purge treats progress only when `removeFirst()` returns `r > 0`, so if every stream’s first chunk is empty (but later chunks hold real payload), one pass removes only those empty chunks with `r == 0`, `changed` stays false, and the code panics.

That situation is not hypothetical: for SSE with an `EventStore` and protocol ≥ 2025-11-25, `streamableServerConn` calls `Append(..., nil)` for the **priming** event so indexes match the wire, which inserts a **zero-length first chunk** per stream. Under memory pressure, purge can hit this path.

**To Reproduce**

Steps to reproduce the behavior:

1. Use `NewMemoryEventStore` with a **small** `MaxBytes` (e.g. `SetMaxBytes(50)` after creation).
2. `Open` a session and stream ID.
3. `Append(nil)` (same as the SDK’s priming append).
4. `Append` a non-empty payload large enough that total stored bytes exceed `MaxBytes` (e.g. 100 bytes).
5. `Append` again with more payload so `purge()` runs while the list still looks like `[nil, …payload…]` with the empty chunk first.

The last `Append` can trigger the panic during `purge()` inside `Append`.

**Expected behavior**

Purge should evict data until `nBytes <= MaxBytes` (or until no evictable data remains) **without panicking**. Removing a leading empty chunk should count as progress so the next iteration can evict non-empty bytes.

**Logs**

Example panic / goroutine header:

```text
panic: no progress during purge

goroutine ... [running]:
github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk/mcp.(*MemoryEventStore).purge(...)
github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk/mcp.(*MemoryEventStore).Append(...)
github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk/mcp.(*streamableServerConn).Write(...)
github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk/internal/jsonrpc2.(*Connection).write(...)
```

**Additional context**

- **Version:** e.g. `github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk` v1.4.1
- **Cause:** `mcp/event.go` `purge()` only sets `changed` when `r > 0` after `removeFirst()`; empty chunks do not increment `nBytes` but still occupy the front of `dataList`.
- **Related code:** `mcp/streamable.go` — SSE priming path stores the priming event via `Append(..., nil)` when `effectiveVersion >= protocolVersion20251125`.
- **Possible fix:** Treat any `removeFirst()` from a `dataList` with `dl.size > 0` as progress, or strip leading empty chunks in a loop until a non-empty eviction or empty list.
- **Workaround for callers:** raise `MaxBytes`, or use a custom `EventStore` implementation until fixed.


</pr_description>

     1	// Copyright 2025 The Go MCP SDK Authors. All rights reserved.
     2	// Use of this source code is governed by an MIT-style

     4	
     5	// This file is for SSE events.
     6	// See https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Server-sent_events/Using_server-sent_events.
     7	
     8	package mcp
     9	
    10	import (
    11	        "bufio"
    12	        "bytes"
    13	        "context"
    14	        "errors"
    15	        "fmt"
    16	        "io"
    17	        "iter"
    18	        "maps"
    19	        "net/http"
    20	        "slices"
    21	        "strings"
    22	        "sync"
    23	)
    24	
    25	// If true, MemoryEventStore will do frequent validation to check invariants, slowing it down.
    26	// Enable for debugging.
    27	const validateMemoryEventStore = false
    28	
    29	// An Event is a server-sent event.
    30	// See https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Server-sent_events/Using_server-sent_events#fields.
    31	type Event struct {
    32	        Name  string // the "event" field
    33	        ID    string // the "id" field
    34	        Data  []byte // the "data" field
    35	        Retry string // the "retry" field
    36	}
    37	
    38	// Empty reports whether the Event is empty.
    39	func (e Event) Empty() bool {
    40	        return e.Name == "" && e.ID == "" && len(e.Data) == 0 && e.Retry == ""
    41	}
    42	
    43	// writeEvent writes the event to w, and flushes.
    44	func writeEvent(w io.Writer, evt Event) (int, error) {
    45	        var b bytes.Buffer
    46	        if evt.Name != "" {
    47	                fmt.Fprintf(&b, "event: %s\n", evt.Name)
    48	        }
    49	        if evt.ID != "" {
    50	                fmt.Fprintf(&b, "id: %s\n", evt.ID)
    51	        }
    52	        if evt.Retry != "" {
    53	                fmt.Fprintf(&b, "retry: %s\n", evt.Retry)
    54	        }
    55	        fmt.Fprintf(&b, "data: %s\n\n", string(evt.Data))
    56	        n, err := w.Write(b.Bytes())
    57	        if f, ok := w.(http.Flusher); ok {
    58	                f.Flush()
    59	        }
    60	        return n, err
    61	}
    62	
    63	// scanEvents iterates SSE events in the given scanner. The iterated error is
    64	// terminal: if encountered, the stream is corrupt or broken and should no
    65	// longer be used.
    66	//
    67	// TODO(rfindley): consider a different API here that makes failure modes more
    68	// apparent.
    69	func scanEvents(r io.Reader) iter.Seq2[Event, error] {
    70	        reader := bufio.NewReader(r)
    71	
    72	        // TODO: investigate proper behavior when events are out of order, or have
    73	        // non-standard names.
    74	        var (
    75	                eventKey = []byte("event")
    76	                idKey    = []byte("id")
    77	                dataKey  = []byte("data")
    78	                retryKey = []byte("retry")
    79	        )
    80	
    81	        return func(yield func(Event, error) bool) {
    82	                // iterate event from the wire.
    83	                // https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Server-sent_events/Using_server-sent_events#examples
    84	                //
    85	                //  - `key: value` line records.
    86	                //  - Consecutive `data: ...` fields are joined with newlines.
    87	                //  - Unrecognized fields are ignored. Since we only care about 'event', 'id', and
    88	                //   'data', these are the only three we consider.
    89	                //  - Lines starting with ":" are ignored.
    90	                //  - Records are terminated with two consecutive newlines.
    91	                var (
    92	                        evt     Event
    93	                        dataBuf *bytes.Buffer // if non-nil, preceding field was also data
    94	                )
    95	                yieldEvent := func() bool {
    96	                        if dataBuf != nil {
    97	                                evt.Data = dataBuf.Bytes()
    98	                                dataBuf = nil
    99	                        }
   100	                        if evt.Empty() {
   101	                                return true
   102	                        }
   103	                        if !yield(evt, nil) {
   104	                                return false
   105	                        }
   106	                        evt = Event{}
   107	                        return true
   108	                }
   109	                for {
   110	                        line, err := reader.ReadBytes('\n')
   111	                        if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {
   112	                                yield(Event{}, fmt.Errorf("error reading event: %v", err))
   113	                                return
   114	                        }
   115	                        line = bytes.TrimRight(line, "\r\n")
   116	                        isEOF := errors.Is(err, io.EOF)
   117	
   118	                        if len(line) == 0 {
   119	                                if !yieldEvent() {
   120	                                        return
   121	                                }
   122	                                if isEOF {
   123	                                        return
   124	                                }
   125	                                continue
   126	                        }
   127	                        before, after, found := bytes.Cut(line, []byte{':'})
   128	                        if !found {
   129	                                yield(Event{}, fmt.Errorf("%w: malformed line in SSE stream: %q", errMalformedEvent, string(line)))
   130	                                return
   131	                        }
   132	                        switch {
   133	                        case bytes.Equal(before, eventKey):
   134	                                evt.Name = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
   135	                        case bytes.Equal(before, idKey):
   136	                                evt.ID = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
   137	                        case bytes.Equal(before, retryKey):
   138	                                evt.Retry = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
   139	                        case bytes.Equal(before, dataKey):
   140	                                data := bytes.TrimSpace(after)
   141	                                if dataBuf == nil {
   142	                                        dataBuf = new(bytes.Buffer)
   143	                                } else {
   144	                                        dataBuf.WriteByte('\n')
   145	                                }
   146	                                dataBuf.Write(data)
   147	                        }
   148	
   149	                        if isEOF {
   150	                                yieldEvent()
   151	                                return
   152	                        }
   153	                }
   154	        }
   155	}
   156	
   157	// An EventStore tracks data for SSE streams.
   158	// A single EventStore suffices for all sessions, since session IDs are
   159	// globally unique. So one EventStore can be created per process, for
   160	// all Servers in the process.
   161	// Such a store is able to bound resource usage for the entire process.
   162	//
   163	// All of an EventStore's methods must be safe for use by multiple goroutines.
   164	type EventStore interface {
   165	        // Open is called when a new stream is created. It may be used to ensure that
   166	        // the underlying data structure for the stream is initialized, making it
   167	        // ready to store and replay event streams.
   168	        Open(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string) error
   169	
   170	        // Append appends data for an outgoing event to given stream, which is part of the
   171	        // given session.
   172	        Append(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string, data []byte) error
   173	
   174	        // After returns an iterator over the data for the given session and stream, beginning
   175	        // just after the given index.
   176	        //
   177	        // Once the iterator yields a non-nil error, it will stop.
   178	        // After's iterator must return an error immediately if any data after index was
   179	        // dropped; it must not return partial results.
   180	        // The stream must have been opened previously (see [EventStore.Open]).
   181	        After(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string, index int) iter.Seq2[[]byte, error]
   182	
   183	        // SessionClosed informs the store that the given session is finished, along
   184	        // with all of its streams.
   185	        //
   186	        // A store cannot rely on this method being called for cleanup. It should institute
   187	        // additional mechanisms, such as timeouts, to reclaim storage.
   188	        SessionClosed(_ context.Context, sessionID string) error
   189	
   190	        // There is no StreamClosed method. A server doesn't know when a stream is finished, because
   191	        // the client can always send a GET with a Last-Event-ID referring to the stream.
   192	}
   193	
   194	// A dataList is a list of []byte.
   195	// The zero dataList is ready to use.
   196	type dataList struct {
   197	        size  int // total size of data bytes
   198	        first int // the stream index of the first element in data
   199	        data  [][]byte
   200	}
   201	
   202	func (dl *dataList) appendData(d []byte) {
   203	        // Empty data consumes memory but doesn't increment size. However, it should
   204	        // be rare.
   205	        dl.data = append(dl.data, d)
   206	        dl.size += len(d)
   207	}
   208	
   209	// removeFirst removes the first data item in dl, returning the size of the item.
   210	// It panics if dl is empty.
   211	func (dl *dataList) removeFirst() int {
   212	        if len(dl.data) == 0 {
   213	                panic("empty dataList")
   214	        }
   215	        r := len(dl.data[0])
   216	        dl.size -= r
   217	        dl.data[0] = nil // help GC
   218	        dl.data = dl.data[1:]
   219	        dl.first++
   220	        return r
   221	}
   222	
   223	// A MemoryEventStore is an [EventStore] backed by memory.
   224	type MemoryEventStore struct {
   225	        mu       sync.Mutex
   226	        maxBytes int                             // max total size of all data
   227	        nBytes   int                             // current total size of all data
   228	        store    map[string]map[string]*dataList // session ID -> stream ID -> *dataList
   229	}
   230	
   231	// MemoryEventStoreOptions are options for a [MemoryEventStore].
   232	type MemoryEventStoreOptions struct{}
   233	
   234	// MaxBytes returns the maximum number of bytes that the store will retain before
   235	// purging data.
   236	func (s *MemoryEventStore) MaxBytes() int {
   237	        s.mu.Lock()
   238	        defer s.mu.Unlock()
   239	        return s.maxBytes
   240	}
   241	
   242	// SetMaxBytes sets the maximum number of bytes the store will retain before purging
   243	// data. The argument must not be negative. If it is zero, a suitable default will be used.
   244	// SetMaxBytes can be called at any time. The size of the store will be adjusted
   245	// immediately.
   246	func (s *MemoryEventStore) SetMaxBytes(n int) {
   247	        s.mu.Lock()
   248	        defer s.mu.Unlock()
   249	        switch {
   250	        case n < 0:
   251	                panic("negative argument")
   252	        case n == 0:
   253	                s.maxBytes = defaultMaxBytes
   254	        default:
   255	                s.maxBytes = n
   256	        }
   257	        s.purge()
   258	}
   259	
   260	const defaultMaxBytes = 10 << 20 // 10 MiB
   261	
   262	// NewMemoryEventStore creates a [MemoryEventStore] with the default value
   263	// for MaxBytes.
   264	func NewMemoryEventStore(opts *MemoryEventStoreOptions) *MemoryEventStore {
   265	        return &MemoryEventStore{
   266	                maxBytes: defaultMaxBytes,
   267	                store:    make(map[string]map[string]*dataList),
   268	        }
   269	}
   270	
   271	// Open implements [EventStore.Open]. It ensures that the underlying data
   272	// structures for the given session are initialized and ready for use.
   273	func (s *MemoryEventStore) Open(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string) error {
   274	        s.mu.Lock()
   275	        defer s.mu.Unlock()
   276	        s.init(sessionID, streamID)
   277	        return nil
   278	}
   279	
   280	// init is an internal helper function that ensures the nested map structure for a
   281	// given sessionID and streamID exists, creating it if necessary. It returns the
   282	// dataList associated with the specified IDs.
   283	// Requires s.mu.
   284	func (s *MemoryEventStore) init(sessionID, streamID string) *dataList {
   285	        streamMap, ok := s.store[sessionID]
   286	        if !ok {
   287	                streamMap = make(map[string]*dataList)
   288	                s.store[sessionID] = streamMap
   289	        }
   290	        dl, ok := streamMap[streamID]
   291	        if !ok {
   292	                dl = &dataList{}
   293	                streamMap[streamID] = dl
   294	        }
   295	        return dl
   296	}
   297	
   298	// Append implements [EventStore.Append] by recording data in memory.
   299	func (s *MemoryEventStore) Append(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string, data []byte) error {
   300	        s.mu.Lock()
   301	        defer s.mu.Unlock()
   302	        dl := s.init(sessionID, streamID)
   303	        // Purge before adding, so at least the current data item will be present.
   304	        // (That could result in nBytes > maxBytes, but we'll live with that.)
   305	        s.purge()
   306	        dl.appendData(data)
   307	        s.nBytes += len(data)
   308	        return nil
   309	}
   310	
   311	// ErrEventsPurged is the error that [EventStore.After] should return if the event just after the
   312	// index is no longer available.
   313	var ErrEventsPurged = errors.New("data purged")
   314	
   315	// errMalformedEvent is returned when an SSE event cannot be parsed due to format violations.
   316	// This is a hard error indicating corrupted data or protocol violations, as opposed to
   317	// transient I/O errors which may be retryable.
   318	var errMalformedEvent = errors.New("malformed event")
   319	
   320	// After implements [EventStore.After].
   321	func (s *MemoryEventStore) After(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string, index int) iter.Seq2[[]byte, error] {
   322	        // Return the data items to yield.
   323	        // We must copy, because dataList.removeFirst nils out slice elements.
   324	        copyData := func() ([][]byte, error) {
   325	                s.mu.Lock()
   326	                defer s.mu.Unlock()
   327	                streamMap, ok := s.store[sessionID]
   328	                if !ok {
   329	                        return nil, fmt.Errorf("MemoryEventStore.After: unknown session ID %q", sessionID)
   330	                }
   331	                dl, ok := streamMap[streamID]
   332	                if !ok {
   333	                        return nil, fmt.Errorf("MemoryEventStore.After: unknown stream ID %v in session %q", streamID, sessionID)
   334	                }
   335	                start := index + 1
   336	                if dl.first > start {
   337	                        return nil, fmt.Errorf("MemoryEventStore.After: index %d, stream ID %v, session %q: %w",
   338	                                index, streamID, sessionID, ErrEventsPurged)
   339	                }
   340	                return slices.Clone(dl.data[start-dl.first:]), nil
   341	        }
   342	
   343	        return func(yield func([]byte, error) bool) {
   344	                ds, err := copyData()
   345	                if err != nil {
   346	                        yield(nil, err)
   347	                        return
   348	                }
   349	                for _, d := range ds {
   350	                        if !yield(d, nil) {
   351	                                return
   352	                        }
   353	                }
   354	        }
   355	}
   356	
   357	// SessionClosed implements [EventStore.SessionClosed].
   358	func (s *MemoryEventStore) SessionClosed(_ context.Context, sessionID string) error {
   359	        s.mu.Lock()
   360	        defer s.mu.Unlock()
   361	        for _, dl := range s.store[sessionID] {
   362	                s.nBytes -= dl.size
   363	        }
   364	        delete(s.store, sessionID)
   365	        s.validate()
   366	        return nil
   367	}
   368	
   369	// purge removes data until no more than s.maxBytes bytes are in use.
   370	// It must be called with s.mu held.
   371	func (s *MemoryEventStore) purge() {
   372	        // Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.
   373	        for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {
   374	                changed := false
   375	                for _, sm := range s.store {
   376	                        for _, dl := range sm {
   377	                                if dl.size > 0 {
   378	                                        r := dl.removeFirst()
   379	                                        if r > 0 {
   380	                                                changed = true
   381	                                                s.nBytes -= r
   382	                                        }
   383	                                }
   384	                        }
   385	                }
   386	                if !changed {
   387	                        panic("no progress during purge")
   388	                }
   389	        }
   390	        s.validate()
   391	}
   392	
   393	// validate checks that the store's data structures are valid.
   394	// It must be called with s.mu held.
   395	func (s *MemoryEventStore) validate() {
   396	        if !validateMemoryEventStore {
   397	                return
   398	        }
   399	        // Check that we're accounting for the size correctly.
   400	        n := 0
   401	        for _, sm := range s.store {
   402	                for _, dl := range sm {
   403	                        for _, d := range dl.data {
   404	                                n += len(d)
   405	                        }
   406	                }
   407	        }
   408	        if n != s.nBytes {
   409	                panic("sizes don't add up")
   410	        }
   411	}
   412	
   413	// debugString returns a string containing the state of s.
   414	// Used in tests.
   415	func (s *MemoryEventStore) debugString() string {
   416	        s.mu.Lock()
   417	        defer s.mu.Unlock()
   418	        var b strings.Builder
   419	        for i, sess := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(s.store)) {
   420	                if i > 0 {
   421	                        fmt.Fprintf(&b, "; ")
   422	                }
   423	                sm := s.store[sess]
   424	                for i, sid := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(sm)) {
   425	                        if i > 0 {
   426	                                fmt.Fprintf(&b, "; ")
   427	                        }
   428	                        dl := sm[sid]
   429	                        fmt.Fprintf(&b, "%s %s first=%d", sess, sid, dl.first)
   430	                        for _, d := range dl.data {
   431	                                fmt.Fprintf(&b, " %s", d)
   432	                        }
   433	                }
   434	        }
   435	        return b.String()
   436	}

2026-05-30 01:08:46,397 - INFO - swea-agent-modelcontextprotocol__go-sdk-862 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I can see the issue clearly. Let me look at the `purge()` function more carefully. The problem is:

1. In `purge()`, it iterates through all streams and tries to `removeFirst()` from streams with `dl.size > 0`.
2. But `removeFirst()` returns the length of the first data element, which could be 0 (empty/nil []byte).
3. `changed` is only set to `true` when `r > 0`.
4. So if every stream's first element is an empty chunk (size 0), `removeFirst()` is called, returns 0, `changed` stays false, and the function panics with "no progress during purge".

Let me create a script to reproduce this

🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro_test.go << 'EOF'
package main

import (
    "context"
    "fmt"
    "github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk/mcp"
)

func main() {
    store := mcp.NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
    store.SetMaxBytes(50)

    ctx := context.Background()
    sessionID := "session1"
    streamID := "stream1"

    // Open the stream
    err := store.Open(ctx, sessionID, streamID)
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Open error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }

    // Step 1: Append(nil) - the priming SSE event
    err = store.Append(ctx, sessionID, streamID, nil)
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Append nil error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }
    fmt.Println("Step 1: Append(nil) succeeded")

    // Step 2: Append a large payload to exceed MaxBytes
    largePayload := make([]byte, 100)
    for i := range largePayload {
        largePayload[i] = byte('a')
    }
    err = store.Append(ctx, sessionID, streamID, largePayload)
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Append large payload error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }
    fmt.Println("Step 2: Append(large) succeeded")

    // Step 3: Append again - this should trigger purge and potentially panic
    err = store.Append(ctx, sessionID, streamID, []byte("hello"))
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Append final error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }
    fmt.Println("Step 3: Append succeeded - no panic!")
}
EOF

I've confirmed the bug. Now let me analyze the `purge()` function and the fix needed.

The issue is in `purge()` at line 371-391:

```go
func (s *MemoryEventStore) purge() {
    for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {
        changed := false
        for _, sm := range s.store {
            for _, dl := range sm {
                if dl.size > 0 {
                    r := dl.removeFirst()
                    if r > 0 {
                        changed = true
                        s.nBytes -= r
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        if !changed {
            panic("no progress during purge")
        }
    }
    s.validate()
}
```

The problem:
1. `dl.size > 0` check: The dataList could have `size > 0` (because there are non-empty items in the list), but the first element could be empty (nil). So `removeFirst()` gets called, returns `r == 0`, `changed` stays false.
2. Also note: if a dataList has `size == 0` but has elements (all empty/nil), then `dl.size > 0` is false and we skip it entirely, but the list still occupies space in memory.

The fix should treat any `removeFirst()` call as progress, because removing an empty chunk makes room to remove the next (non-empty) chunk in the next iteration. Also, we should consider dataLists that have `dl.size == 0` but still have elements - those should also be purged.

Let me think about the right fix:

Option 1: Change `changed` to be set whenever we call `removeFirst()`, regardless of `r`. Also, we should also try to remove empty leading elements from dataLists even if `dl.size == 0` (i.e., all elements are empty).

Actually, let me re-examine. If `dl.size == 0`, that means all elements in the dataList are empty (nil). We should still remove them because they consume memory (the slice headers). But `s.nBytes` won't decrease because `r == 0`.

But wait, the loop condition is `s.nBytes > s.maxBytes`. If all elements are empty, `s.nBytes` won't decrease, and we'd loop forever. So we need a different approach.

Actually, the fix described in the PR says:
- Treat any `removeFirst()` from a `dataList` with `dl.size > 0` as progress, or strip leading empty chunks in a loop until a non-empty eviction or empty list.

Let me think more carefully...

The key insight: when `dl.size > 0`, the dataList has at least some non-empty data. If the first element is empty, removing it counts as progress because it allows us to eventually get to the non-empty data in subsequent iterations.

But we also need to handle the case where `dl.size == 0` but `len(dl.data) > 0` - i.e., the dataList has only empty elements. In this case, we should remove them too (to free memory), but since `s.nBytes` won't decrease, we could infinite loop. So we need to handle this case differently - perhaps by removing all empty leading elements in one go, or by checking if there are any remaining elements.

Let me look at how `dataList` works again:

```go
type dataList struct {
    size  int // total size of data bytes
    first int // the stream index of the first element in data
    data  [][]byte
}
```

`size` is the total bytes of all data in the list. Empty/nil elements contribute 0 to `size`.

So the fix should:
1. When `dl.size > 0`, call `removeFirst()` and always count it as progress (since we're removing something from the front, even if it's empty, making progress toward the non-empty data).
2. When `dl.size == 0` but `len(dl.data) > 0`, we should also remove elements (they're all empty), and count it as progress.

But wait - if we have a dataList with only empty elements, `s.nBytes` won't change, and we'll loop forever. However, we'll eventually have `len(dl.data) == 0` for all dataLists, and then `changed` will be false and we'll panic again.

Hmm, let me reconsider. The loop condition is `s.nBytes > s.maxBytes`. If `s.nBytes > s.maxBytes`, then there must be at least some non-empty data somewhere. So there must be some dataList with `dl.size > 0`. But the first element of that dataList might be empty. So we need to handle the case where a dataList with `dl.size > 0` has an empty first element.

The simplest fix: in `purge()`, when `dl.size > 0`, we should keep calling `removeFirst()` until we either get a non-zero `r` or the dataList becomes empty. But that's a bit complex.

Actually, the simplest fix as suggested by the PR: treat any `removeFirst()` as progress when `dl.size > 0`. But we also need to handle the `s.nBytes -= r` correctly (subtracting 0 is fine).

But there's still another subtlety: if `dl.size > 0`, we call `removeFirst()`, get `r == 0`, set `changed = true`, but `s.nBytes -= 0` does nothing. Next iteration of the outer loop, same thing could happen if there are multiple leading empty elements. Eventually we'll get to a non-empty element and reduce `s.nBytes`.

But wait, what if after removing all leading empty elements from all dataLists, we still haven't reduced `s.nBytes`? Then in the next outer loop iteration, all dataLists with `dl.size > 0` will have non-empty first elements, and `removeFirst()` will return `r > 0`, reducing `s.nBytes`. So the fix works.

But there's another edge case: what if `dl.size == 0` but `len(dl.data) > 0`? In this case, the dataList has only empty elements. These don't contribute to `s.nBytes`, so the loop condition `s.nBytes > s.maxBytes` must be satisfied by other dataLists. But we should still clean up empty dataLists. However, if we only process dataLists with `dl.size > 0`, we'll skip these. That's probably fine because they don't contribute to `nBytes`.

Actually, there's still a problem: if we have a dataList with `dl.size > 0` but all its data is after many leading empty elements, we keep removing empty elements one by one, each time `changed = true` but `s.nBytes` doesn't decrease. We could have many iterations of the outer loop. But that's fine; it's just a bit slow, and the PR says this is rare.

	// Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.
	for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {
		changed := false
		for _, sm := range s.store {

package main

import (
    "context"
    "fmt"
    "github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk/mcp"
)

func main() {
    ctx := context.Background()
    
    // Test 1: Basic scenario from PR description
    fmt.Println("=== Test 1: Basic scenario ===")
    store := mcp.NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
    store.SetMaxBytes(50)
    
    store.Open(ctx, "s1", "st1")
    store.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", nil)                    // priming empty
    store.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", make([]byte, 100))      // large payload
    store.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", []byte("hello"))        // triggers purge
    fmt.Println("Test 1 passed!")
    
    // Test 2: Multiple leading empty elements
    fmt.Println("=== Test 2: Multiple leading empty elements ===")
    store2 := mcp.NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
    store2.SetMaxBytes(50)
    
    store2.Open(ctx, "s1", "st1")
    store2.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", nil)
    store2.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", nil)
    store2.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", nil)
    store2.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", make([]byte, 100))
    store2.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", []byte("hello"))
    fmt.Println("Test 2 passed!")
    
    // Test 3: Multiple streams, each with leading empty
    fmt.Println("=== Test 3: Multiple streams with leading empty ===")
    store3 := mcp.NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
    store3.SetMaxBytes(50)
    
    store3.Open(ctx, "s1", "st1")
    store3.Open(ctx, "s1", "st2")
    store3.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", nil)
    store3.Append(ctx, "s1", "st2", nil)
    store3.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", make([]byte, 100))
    store3.Append(ctx, "s1", "st2", make([]byte, 100))
    store3.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", []byte("hello"))
    fmt.Println("Test 3 passed!")
    
    // Test 4: Only empty elements (size == 0 but data present)
    fmt.Println("=== Test 4: Only empty elements ===")
    store4 := mcp.NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
    store4.SetMaxBytes(0)  // set to default (10MB), can't test purge with only empty
    // Instead, let's just verify we can append only empty elements and then close
    store4.SetMaxBytes(50)
    store4.Open(ctx, "s1", "st1")
    store4.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", nil)
    store4.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", nil)
    // Add some real data to trigger purge
    store4.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", make([]byte, 100))
    store4.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", []byte("hello"))
    fmt.Println("Test 4 passed!")
    
    // Test 5: Normal operation without empty elements
    fmt.Println("=== Test 5: Normal operation ===")
    store5 := mcp.NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
    store5.SetMaxBytes(50)
    
    store5.Open(ctx, "s1", "st1")
    store5.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", []byte("data1"))
    store5.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", make([]byte, 100))
    store5.Append(ctx, "s1", "st1", []byte("data2"))
    fmt.Println("Test 5 passed!")
    
    fmt.Println("\nAll tests passed!")
}

    17	func TestScanEvents(t *testing.T) {
    18	        tests := []struct {
    19	                name    string
    20	                input   string
    21	                want    []Event
    22	                wantErr string
    23	        }{
    24	                {
    25	                        name:  "simple event",
    26	                        input: "event: message\nid: 1\ndata: hello\n\n",
    27	                        want: []Event{
    28	                                {Name: "message", ID: "1", Data: []byte("hello")},
    29	                        },
    30	                },
    31	                {
    32	                        name:  "multiple data lines",
    33	                        input: "data: line 1\ndata: line 2\n\n",
    34	                        want: []Event{
    35	                                {Data: []byte("line 1\nline 2")},
    36	                        },
    37	                },
    38	                {
    39	                        name:  "multiple events",
    40	                        input: "data: first\n\nevent: second\ndata: second\n\n",
    41	                        want: []Event{
    42	                                {Data: []byte("first")},
    43	                                {Name: "second", Data: []byte("second")},
    44	                        },
    45	                },
    46	                {
    47	                        name:  "no trailing newline",
    48	                        input: "data: hello",
    49	                        want: []Event{
    50	                                {Data: []byte("hello")},
    51	                        },
    52	                },
    53	                {
    54	                        name:    "malformed line",
    55	                        input:   "invalid line\n\n",
    56	                        wantErr: "malformed line",
    57	                },
    58	                {
    59	                        name:  "message with 2 data lines and another event",
    60	                        input: "event: message\ndata: hello\ndata: hello\ndata: hello\n\nevent:keepalive",
    61	                        want: []Event{
    62	                                {Name: "message", Data: []byte("hello\nhello\nhello")},
    63	                                {Name: "keepalive"},
    64	                        },
    65	                },
    66	                {
    67	                        name:  "event with multiple lines",
    68	                        input: "event: message\ndata: hello\ndata: hello\ndata: hello\nid:1",
    69	                        want: []Event{
    70	                                {Name: "message", ID: "1", Data: []byte("hello\nhello\nhello")},
    71	                        },
    72	                },
    73	                {
    74	                        name: "multiple events, out of order keys",
    75	                        input: strings.Join([]string{
    76	                                "event:message",
    77	                                "data: hello0",
    78	                                "\n",
    79	                                "data: hello1",
    80	                                "data: hello1",
    81	                                "id:1",
    82	                                "event:message",
    83	                                "\n",
    84	                                "event:message",
    85	                                "data: hello3",
    86	                                "data: hello3",
    87	                                "id:3",
    88	                                "\n",
    89	                                "data: hello4",
    90	                                "data: hello4",
    91	                                "id:4",
    92	                                "event:message",
    93	                        }, "\n"),
    94	                        want: []Event{
    95	                                {Name: "message", Data: []byte("hello0")},
    96	                                {Name: "message", ID: "1", Data: []byte("hello1\nhello1")},
    97	                                {Name: "message", ID: "3", Data: []byte("hello3\nhello3")},
    98	                                {Name: "message", ID: "4", Data: []byte("hello4\nhello4")},
    99	                        },
   100	                },
   101	                {
   102	                        name:  "non-continuous data items in the event",
   103	                        input: "event: foo\ndata: 123\nretry: 5\ndata: 456",
   104	                        want: []Event{
   105	                                {Name: "foo", Data: []byte("123\n456"), Retry: "5"},
   106	                        },
   107	                },
   108	                {
   109	                        name:  "no-data events",
   110	                        input: "event: foo\n\nevent: bar",
   111	                        want: []Event{
   112	                                {Name: "foo"},
   113	                                {Name: "bar"},
   114	                        },
   115	                },
   116	                {
   117	                        name:  "empty data event",
   118	                        input: "event: foo\ndata:\n\nevent: bar",
   119	                        want: []Event{
   120	                                {Name: "foo"},
   121	                                {Name: "bar"},
   122	                        },
   123	                },
   124	                {
   125	
   126	                        name:    "malformed data event",
   127	                        input:   "someline",
   128	                        wantErr: "malformed event",
   129	                },
   130	        }
   131	
   132	        for _, tt := range tests {
   133	                t.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {
   134	                        r := strings.NewReader(tt.input)
   135	                        var got []Event
   136	                        var err error
   137	                        for e, err2 := range scanEvents(r) {
   138	                                if err2 != nil {
   139	                                        err = err2
   140	                                        break
   141	                                }
   142	                                got = append(got, e)
   143	                        }
   144	
   145	                        if tt.wantErr != "" {
   146	                                if err == nil {
   147	                                        t.Fatalf("scanEvents() got nil error, want error containing %q", tt.wantErr)
   148	                                }
   149	                                if !strings.Contains(err.Error(), tt.wantErr) {
   150	                                        t.Fatalf("scanEvents() error = %q, want containing %q", err, tt.wantErr)
   151	                                }
   152	                                return
   153	                        }
   154	
   155	                        if err != nil {
   156	                                t.Fatalf("scanEvents() returned unexpected error: %v", err)
   157	                        }
   158	
   159	                        if len(got) != len(tt.want) {
   160	                                t.Fatalf("scanEvents() got %d events, want %d", len(got), len(tt.want))
   161	                        }
   162	
   163	                        for i := range got {
   164	                                if g, w := got[i].Name, tt.want[i].Name; g != w {
   165	                                        t.Errorf("event %d: name = %q, want %q", i, g, w)
   166	                                }
   167	                                if g, w := got[i].ID, tt.want[i].ID; g != w {
   168	                                        t.Errorf("event %d: id = %q, want %q", i, g, w)
   169	                                }
   170	                                if g, w := string(got[i].Data), string(tt.want[i].Data); g != w {
   171	                                        t.Errorf("event %d: data = %q, want %q", i, g, w)
   172	                                }
   173	                        }
   174	                })
   175	        }

   178	func TestMemoryEventStoreState(t *testing.T) {
   179	        ctx := context.Background()
   180	
   181	        appendEvent := func(s *MemoryEventStore, sess, stream string, data string) {
   182	                if err := s.Append(ctx, sess, stream, []byte(data)); err != nil {
   183	                        t.Fatal(err)
   184	                }
   185	        }
   186	
   187	        for _, tt := range []struct {
   188	                name     string
   189	                actions  func(*MemoryEventStore)
   190	                want     string // output of debugString
   191	                wantSize int    // value of nBytes
   192	        }{
   193	                {
   194	                        "appends",
   195	                        func(s *MemoryEventStore) {
   196	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d1")
   197	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d2")
   198	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d3")
   199	                                appendEvent(s, "S2", "8", "d4")
   200	                        },
   201	                        "S1 1 first=0 d1 d3; S1 2 first=0 d2; S2 8 first=0 d4",
   202	                        8,
   203	                },
   204	                {
   205	                        "session close",
   206	                        func(s *MemoryEventStore) {
   207	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d1")
   208	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d2")
   209	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d3")
   210	                                appendEvent(s, "S2", "8", "d4")
   211	                                s.SessionClosed(ctx, "S1")
   212	                        },
   213	                        "S2 8 first=0 d4",
   214	                        2,
   215	                },
   216	                {
   217	                        "purge",
   218	                        func(s *MemoryEventStore) {
   219	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d1")
   220	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d2")
   221	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d3")
   222	                                appendEvent(s, "S2", "8", "d4")
   223	                                // We are using 8 bytes (d1,d2, d3, d4).
   224	                                // To purge 6, we remove the first of each stream, leaving only d3.
   225	                                s.SetMaxBytes(2)
   226	                        },
   227	                        // The other streams remain, because we may add to them.
   228	                        "S1 1 first=1 d3; S1 2 first=1; S2 8 first=1",
   229	                        2,
   230	                },
   231	                {
   232	                        "purge append",
   233	                        func(s *MemoryEventStore) {
   234	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d1")
   235	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d2")
   236	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d3")
   237	                                appendEvent(s, "S2", "8", "d4")
   238	                                s.SetMaxBytes(2)
   239	                                // Up to here, identical to the "purge" case.
   240	                                // Each of these additions will result in a purge.
   241	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d5") // remove d3
   242	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d6") // remove d5
   243	                        },
   244	                        "S1 1 first=2; S1 2 first=2 d6; S2 8 first=1",
   245	                        2,
   246	                },
   247	                {
   248	                        "purge resize append",
   249	                        func(s *MemoryEventStore) {
   250	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d1")
   251	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d2")
   252	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "1", "d3")
   253	                                appendEvent(s, "S2", "8", "d4")
   254	                                s.SetMaxBytes(2)
   255	                                // Up to here, identical to the "purge" case.
   256	                                s.SetMaxBytes(6) // make room
   257	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d5")
   258	                                appendEvent(s, "S1", "2", "d6")
   259	                        },
   260	                        // The other streams remain, because we may add to them.
   261	                        "S1 1 first=1 d3; S1 2 first=1 d5 d6; S2 8 first=1",
   262	                        6,
   263	                },
   264	        } {
   265	                t.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {
   266	                        s := NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
   267	                        tt.actions(s)
   268	                        got := s.debugString()
   269	                        if got != tt.want {
   270	                                t.Errorf("\ngot  %s\nwant %s", got, tt.want)
   271	                        }
   272	                        if g, w := s.nBytes, tt.wantSize; g != w {
   273	                                t.Errorf("got size %d, want %d", g, w)
   274	                        }
   275	                })
   276	        }
   277	}

   279	func TestMemoryEventStoreAfter(t *testing.T) {
   280	        ctx := context.Background()
   281	        s := NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
   282	        s.SetMaxBytes(4)
   283	        s.Append(ctx, "S1", "1", []byte("d1"))
   284	        s.Append(ctx, "S1", "1", []byte("d2"))
   285	        s.Append(ctx, "S1", "1", []byte("d3"))
   286	        s.Append(ctx, "S1", "2", []byte("d4")) // will purge d1
   287	        want := "S1 1 first=1 d2 d3; S1 2 first=0 d4"
   288	        if got := s.debugString(); got != want {
   289	                t.Fatalf("got state %q, want %q", got, want)
   290	        }
   291	
   292	        for _, tt := range []struct {
   293	                sessionID string
   294	                streamID  string
   295	                index     int
   296	                want      []string
   297	                wantErr   string // if non-empty, error should contain this string
   298	        }{
   299	                {"S1", "1", 0, []string{"d2", "d3"}, ""},
   300	                {"S1", "1", 1, []string{"d3"}, ""},
   301	                {"S1", "1", 2, nil, ""},
   302	                {"S1", "2", 0, nil, ""},
   303	                {"S1", "3", 0, nil, "unknown stream ID"},
   304	                {"S2", "0", 0, nil, "unknown session ID"},
   305	        } {
   306	                t.Run(fmt.Sprintf("%s-%s-%d", tt.sessionID, tt.streamID, tt.index), func(t *testing.T) {
   307	                        var got []string
   308	                        for d, err := range s.After(ctx, tt.sessionID, tt.streamID, tt.index) {
   309	                                if err != nil {
   310	                                        if tt.wantErr == "" {
   311	                                                t.Fatalf("unexpected error %q", err)
   312	                                        } else if g := err.Error(); !strings.Contains(g, tt.wantErr) {
   313	                                                t.Fatalf("got error %q, want it to contain %q", g, tt.wantErr)
   314	                                        } else {
   315	                                                return
   316	                                        }
   317	                                }
   318	                                got = append(got, string(d))
   319	                        }
   320	                        if tt.wantErr != "" {
   321	                                t.Fatalf("expected error containing %q, got nil", tt.wantErr)
   322	                        }
   323	                        if !slices.Equal(got, tt.want) {
   324	                                t.Errorf("got %v, want %v", got, tt.want)
   325	                        }
   326	                })
   327	        }
   328	}

   330	func BenchmarkMemoryEventStore(b *testing.B) {
   331	        // Benchmark with various settings for event store size, number of session,
   332	        // and payload size.
   333	        //
   334	        // Assume a small number of streams per session, which is probably realistic.
   335	        tests := []struct {
   336	                name     string
   337	                limit    int
   338	                sessions int
   339	                datasize int
   340	        }{
   341	                {"1KB", 1024, 1, 16},
   342	                {"1MB", 1024 * 1024, 10, 16},
   343	                {"10MB", 10 * 1024 * 1024, 100, 16},
   344	                {"10MB_big", 10 * 1024 * 1024, 1000, 128},
   345	        }
   346	
   347	        for _, test := range tests {
   348	                b.Run(test.name, func(b *testing.B) {
   349	                        store := NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
   350	                        store.SetMaxBytes(test.limit)
   351	                        ctx := context.Background()
   352	                        sessionIDs := make([]string, test.sessions)
   353	                        streamIDs := make([][3]string, test.sessions)
   354	                        for i := range sessionIDs {
   355	                                sessionIDs[i] = fmt.Sprint(i)
   356	                                for j := range 3 {
   357	                                        streamIDs[i][j] = rand.Text()
   358	                                }
   359	                        }
   360	                        payload := make([]byte, test.datasize)
   361	                        start := time.Now()
   362	                        b.ResetTimer()
   363	                        for i := range b.N {
   364	                                sessionID := sessionIDs[i%len(sessionIDs)]
   365	                                streamID := streamIDs[i%len(sessionIDs)][i%3]
   366	                                store.Append(ctx, sessionID, streamID, payload)
   367	                        }
   368	                        b.ReportMetric(float64(test.datasize)*float64(b.N)/time.Since(start).Seconds(), "bytes/s")
   369	                })
   370	        }
   371	}

```go
func (s *MemoryEventStore) Append(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string, data []byte) error {
    s.mu.Lock()
    defer s.mu.Unlock()
    dl := s.init(sessionID, streamID)
    // Purge before adding, so at least the current data item will be present.
    s.purge()
    dl.appendData(data)
    s.nBytes += len(data)
    return nil
}
```

And `appendData`:
```go
func (dl *dataList) appendData(d []byte) {
    dl.data = append(dl.data, d)
    dl.size += len(d)
}
```

So `s.nBytes` is incremented by `len(data)` and `dl.size` is incremented by `len(d)`. These are consistent. And `SessionClosed` also uses `dl.size` to decrement `s.nBytes`:

```go
func (s *MemoryEventStore) SessionClosed(_ context.Context, sessionID string) error {
    s.mu.Lock()
    defer s.mu.Unlock()
    for _, dl := range s.store[sessionID] {
        s.nBytes -= dl.size
    }
    delete(s.store, sessionID)
    ...
}
```

So `s.nBytes` should always equal the sum of all `dl.size`. The `validate()` function checks this when enabled. So the edge case I was worried about can't happen.

Now let me also consider: what about the `else if` branch I added for `len(dl.data) > 0` when `dl.size == 0`? This handles dataLists that have only empty (nil) entries. > **Possible fix:** Treat any `removeFirst()` from a `dataList` with `dl.size > 0` as progress, or strip leading empty chunks in a loop until a non-empty eviction or empty list.

The minimal fix is just:

```go
if dl.size > 0 {
    r := dl.removeFirst()
    changed = true
    s.nBytes -= r
}
```

This is sufficient because:
1. If `dl.size > 0`, there's non-empty data somewhere in the list.
2. Even if the first element is empty (`r == 0`), removing it counts as progress because it moves us closer to the non-empty data.
3. `s.nBytes -= 0` is a no-op, but `changed = true` ensures we don't panic.

The `else if` branch I added is extra defensive cleanup that doesn't hurt but isn't strictly necessary. Let me keep it since it's harmless and helps clean up memory from empty-only dataLists.

But actually, there's a subtle issue with the `else if` branch: if we have a dataList with only empty entries, and `s.nBytes > s.maxBytes` (due to other streams), we'd remove one empty entry, set `changed = true`, but `s.nBytes` doesn't decrease. This could lead to many unnecessary iterations. However, this is an extremely rare edge case (empty-only dataLists during purge), and each iteration is cheap. So it's fine.

   371	func (s *MemoryEventStore) purge() {
   372	        // Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.
   373	        for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {

+        // TODO: investigate proper behavior when events are out of order, or have

+                idKey    = []byte("id")
+                dataKey  = []byte("data")
+                retryKey = []byte("retry")
+        )
+
+        return func(yield func(Event, error) bool) {
+                // iterate event from the wire.
+                // https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Server-sent_events/Using_server-sent_events#examples
+                //
+                //  - `key: value` line records.
+                //  - Consecutive `data: ...` fields are joined with newlines.
+                //  - Unrecognized fields are ignored. Since we only care about 'event', 'id', and
+                //   'data', these are the only three we consider.
+                //  - Lines starting with ":" are ignored.
+                //  - Records are terminated with two consecutive newlines.
+                var (
+                        evt     Event
+                        dataBuf *bytes.Buffer // if non-nil, preceding field was also data
+                )
+                yieldEvent := func() bool {
+                        if dataBuf != nil {
+                                evt.Data = dataBuf.Bytes()
+                                dataBuf = nil
+                        }
+                        if evt.Empty() {
+                                return true
+                        }
+                        if !yield(evt, nil) {
+                                return false
+                        }
+                        evt = Event{}
+                        return true
+                }
+                for {
+                        line, err := reader.ReadBytes('\n')
+                        if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {
+                                yield(Event{}, fmt.Errorf("error reading event: %v", err))
+                                return
+                        }
+                        line = bytes.TrimRight(line, "\r\n")
+                        isEOF := errors.Is(err, io.EOF)
+
+                        if len(line) == 0 {
+                                if !yieldEvent() {
+                                        return
+                                }
+                                if isEOF {
+                                        return
+                                }
+                                continue
+                        }
+                        before, after, found := bytes.Cut(line, []byte{':'})
+                        if !found {
+                                yield(Event{}, fmt.Errorf("%w: malformed line in SSE stream: %q", errMalformedEvent, string(line)))
+                                return
+                        }
+                        switch {
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, eventKey):
+                                evt.Name = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, idKey):
+                                evt.ID = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, retryKey):
+                                evt.Retry = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, dataKey):
+                                data := bytes.TrimSpace(after)
+                                if dataBuf == nil {
+                                        dataBuf = new(bytes.Buffer)
+                                } else {
+                                        dataBuf.WriteByte('\n')
+                                }
+                                dataBuf.Write(data)
+                        }
+
+                        if isEOF {
+                                yieldEvent()
+                                return
+                        }
+                }
+        }
 }

+        Append(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string, data []byte) error
+

+        // just after the given index.
+        //
+        // Once the iterator yields a non-nil error, it will stop.
+        // After's iterator must return an error immediately if any data after index was
+        // dropped; it must not return partial results.
+        // The stream must have been opened previously (see [EventStore.Open]).
+        After(_ context.Context, sessionID, streamID string, index int) iter.Seq2[[]byte, error]
+
+        // SessionClosed informs the store that the given session is finished, along
+        // with all of its streams.
+        //
+        // A store cannot rely on this method being called for cleanup. It should institute
+        // additional mechanisms, such as timeouts, to reclaim storage.
+        SessionClosed(_ context.Context, sessionID string) error
+
+        // There is no StreamClosed method. A server doesn't know when a stream is finished, because
+        // the client can always send a GET with a Last-Event-ID referring to the stream.

+                changed := false
+                for _, sm := range s.store {
+                        for _, dl := range sm {

+                                        r := dl.removeFirst()
+                                        changed = true
+                                        s.nBytes -= r
+                                } else if len(dl.data) > 0 {

+                                        changed = true
+                                }

+                }
+                if !changed {
+                        panic("no progress during purge")
+                }
+        }

+        return func(yield func(Event, error) bool) {
+                // iterate event from the wire.
+                // https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Server-sent_events/Using_server-sent_events#examples
+                //
+                //  - `key: value` line records.
+                //  - Consecutive `data: ...` fields are joined with newlines.
+                //  - Unrecognized fields are ignored. Since we only care about 'event', 'id', and
+                //   'data', these are the only three we consider.
+                //  - Lines starting with ":" are ignored.
+                //  - Records are terminated with two consecutive newlines.
+                var (
+                        evt     Event
+                        dataBuf *bytes.Buffer // if non-nil, preceding field was also data
+                )
+                yieldEvent := func() bool {
+                        if dataBuf != nil {
+                                evt.Data = dataBuf.Bytes()
+                                dataBuf = nil
+                        }
+                        if evt.Empty() {
+                                return true
+                        }
+                        if !yield(evt, nil) {
+                                return false
+                        }
+                        evt = Event{}
+                        return true
+                }
+                for {
+                        line, err := reader.ReadBytes('\n')
+                        if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {
+                                yield(Event{}, fmt.Errorf("error reading event: %v", err))
+                                return
+                        }
+                        line = bytes.TrimRight(line, "\r\n")
+                        isEOF := errors.Is(err, io.EOF)
+
+                        if len(line) == 0 {
+                                if !yieldEvent() {
+                                        return
+                                }
+                                if isEOF {
+                                        return
+                                }
+                                continue
+                        }
+                        before, after, found := bytes.Cut(line, []byte{':'})
+                        if !found {
+                                yield(Event{}, fmt.Errorf("%w: malformed line in SSE stream: %q", errMalformedEvent, string(line)))
+                                return
+                        }
+                        switch {
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, eventKey):
+                                evt.Name = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, idKey):
+                                evt.ID = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, retryKey):
+                                evt.Retry = strings.TrimSpace(string(after))
+                        case bytes.Equal(before, dataKey):
+                                data := bytes.TrimSpace(after)
+                                if dataBuf == nil {
+                                        dataBuf = new(bytes.Buffer)
+                                } else {
+                                        dataBuf.WriteByte('\n')
+                                }
+                                dataBuf.Write(data)
+                        }
+
+                        if isEOF {
+                                yieldEvent()
+                                return
+                        }
+                }
+        }
 }

 // purge removes data until no more than s.maxBytes bytes are in use.
 // It must be called with s.mu held.
 func (s *MemoryEventStore) purge() {
-	// Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.
-	for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {
-		changed := false
-		for _, sm := range s.store {
-			for _, dl := range sm {
-				if dl.size > 0 {
-					r := dl.removeFirst()
-					if r > 0 {
-						changed = true
-						s.nBytes -= r
-					}
-				}
-			}
-		}
-		if !changed {
-			panic("no progress during purge")
-		}
-	}
-	s.validate()
+        // Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.
+        for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {
+                changed := false
+                for _, sm := range s.store {
+                        for _, dl := range sm {
+                                if dl.size > 0 {
+                                        r := dl.removeFirst()
+                                        changed = true
+                                        s.nBytes -= r
+                                } else if len(dl.data) > 0 {
+                                        // The dataList has only empty (nil) entries that
+                                        // do not contribute to nBytes but still consume
+                                        // memory. Remove them to free space.
+                                        dl.removeFirst()
+                                        changed = true
+                                }
+                        }
+                }
+                if !changed {
+                        panic("no progress during purge")
+                }
+        }
+        s.validate()
 }

   371	func (s *MemoryEventStore) purge() {
   372	        // Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.
   373	        for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {

// It must be called with s.mu held.
func (s *MemoryEventStore) purge() {
	// Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.
	for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {
		changed := false
		for _, sm := range s.store {
			for _, dl := range sm {
				if dl.size > 0 {
					r := dl.removeFirst()
					changed = true
					s.nBytes -= r
				} else if len(dl.data) > 0 {
					// The dataList has only empty (nil) entries that
					// do not contribute to nBytes but still consume
					// memory. Remove them to free space.
					dl.removeFirst()
					changed = true
				}
			}
		}
		if !changed {
			panic("no progress during purge")
		}
	}
	s.validate()
}'

// purge removes data until no more than s.maxBytes bytes are in use.$
// It must be called with s.mu held.$
func (s *MemoryEventStore) purge() {$
        // Remove the first element of every dataList until below the max.$
        for s.nBytes > s.maxBytes {$
                changed := false$
                for _, sm := range s.store {$
                        for _, dl := range sm {$
                                if dl.size > 0 {$
                                        r := dl.removeFirst()$
                                        changed = true$
                                        s.nBytes -= r$
                                } else if len(dl.data) > 0 {$
                                        // The dataList has only empty (nil) entries that$
                                        // do not contribute to nBytes but still consume$
                                        // memory. Remove them to free space.$
                                        dl.removeFirst()$
                                        changed = true$
                                }$
                        }$
                }$
                if !changed {$
                        panic("no progress during purge")$
                }$
        }$
        s.validate()$
}$

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro.go << 'EOF'
package main

import (
    "context"
    "fmt"
    "github.com/modelcontextprotocol/go-sdk/mcp"
)

func main() {
    store := mcp.NewMemoryEventStore(nil)
    store.SetMaxBytes(50)

    ctx := context.Background()
    sessionID := "session1"
    streamID := "stream1"

    // Open the stream
    err := store.Open(ctx, sessionID, streamID)
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Open error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }

    // Step 1: Append(nil) - the priming SSE event
    err = store.Append(ctx, sessionID, streamID, nil)
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Append nil error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }
    fmt.Println("Step 1: Append(nil) succeeded")

    // Step 2: Append a large payload to exceed MaxBytes
    largePayload := make([]byte, 100)
    for i := range largePayload {
        largePayload[i] = byte('a')
    }
    err = store.Append(ctx, sessionID, streamID, largePayload)
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Append large payload error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }
    fmt.Println("Step 2: Append(large) succeeded")

    // Step 3: Append again - this should trigger purge and potentially panic
    err = store.Append(ctx, sessionID, streamID, []byte("hello"))
    if err != nil {
        fmt.Printf("Append final error: %v\n", err)
        return
    }
    fmt.Println("Step 3: Append succeeded - no panic!")
}
EOF
